Important News

He Yingqin Arrives in Jiujiang

▲Leaves for Nanchang by Special Train on the Morning of the 4th

Jiujiang Dispatch: Minister of Military Affairs He Yingqin arrived in Jiujiang at 4:35 PM on the 3rd, after traveling west on the Yong Sui warship from Nanjing on the morning of the 2nd. The ship anchored in Dongliu that evening. Due to heavy fog on the morning of the 3rd, the ship did not set sail until 11:00 AM. Local welcoming personnel had been waiting at the Xun'an Wharf of the Sanbei Company, including Chief of Staff Xie Muhan of the Ninth Route Army, Chief of Staff Guo of the Fifth Division, Provincial Government Committee Members Jiang Ji, Gong Boxun, Huang Bozhong, Yang Mianzhong, Provincial Party Committee Member Liu Zhenqun, He Renhao, Nanxun Railway Bureau Director Yang Zhizhang, Chuqian Warship Captain Zheng Yaogong, Chief of the Second Regiment of the Anti-Smuggling Bureau Gu Baoding, and representatives from all sectors of Jiujiang, including Wang Shirong, Liu Dun, and Peng Keqin, totaling several dozen people. After the Yong Sui warship docked, Minister He raised his hand in salute to the welcoming personnel on the deck, and then went inside to meet with Xie Muhan and the various members of the provincial government and provincial party committee. He first received Lu Diping's report and a map of the bandit areas in the province from Xie Muhan, examining them carefully and inquiring in detail about the bandit situation in Jiangxi. The remaining welcoming personnel were received by Adjutant Wang Renjun, who stated that Minister He had caught a cold before leaving Nanjing and, urged by the Commander-in-Chief, had insisted on traveling while ill. He was not feeling well today, and had ordered him to thank all comrades on his behalf. Minister He's visit to Jiangxi was to eliminate the communist bandits within the set time limit, and he was not expected to leave Jiangxi in the short term.

After meeting with the representatives, He rested on the ship for the night as it was late. He disembarked at 8:30 AM on the 4th, and traveled by car to the railway station. Security along the way was very tight. The special train left for Nanchang at 9:00 AM. The welcoming personnel from the province who had come to Jiujiang all returned to the province with He. (4th)

Sun Lianzhong's Troops to Enter Jiangxi

▲Transportation Scheduled to Begin on the 3rd of This Month

▲The Vanguard Unit is Gao Shuxun's Troops

Jinan Dispatch: The Thirteenth Route Army, led by Sun Lianzhong, has received orders from the Central Government to move to Jiangxi to suppress the communists. Preparations have been underway for many days. Yesterday, Jiang Bocheng told this reporter that Commander Sun had decided to lead his troops to Jiangxi and had scheduled departure for the 3rd, first heading to Jiujiang and then awaiting orders from the Central Government. The Jinpu Railway Administration, under orders from the Central Government, has prepared seven military train sets, one from Jinan and six from Pukou, all of which have been sent to Jining in preparation for transporting Sun's troops. The defense duties of Caozhou and Jining will be filled by troops dispatched by Chairman Han, but the specific units have not yet been determined. According to military sources, the vanguard unit of Sun's troops to enter Jiangxi is the 36th Division under Gao Shuxun. This unit has already completed its organization and will begin transportation tomorrow. Subsequent troops will be led by Sun, and their vacated positions will be filled by a brigade dispatched by the Third Route Army, although the specific unit has not been designated. (February 2nd)

Preservation of the Haiyuan Pavilion Collection

▲The Government Presents Three Options

▲The Yang Family is Still Considering

Jinan Dispatch: The collection of the Haiyuan Pavilion in Liaocheng, owned by the Yang family, is of great significance to China's cultural heritage. Due to the Yang family's continuous sales of the collection, the need for preservation measures is increasingly recognized by society. Much of the Yang family's collection was lost during the Nian Rebellion. However, when the Yang family registered the collection with the government in the first year of the Xuantong reign of the Qing Dynasty in order to preserve it, it still included the following books: (1) the Haiyuan Pavilion Book Catalog in six volumes, totaling 3,236 titles in the four categories of classics, history, philosophy, and literature, comprising over 208,300 volumes; (2) a catalog of Song and Yuan dynasty books in one volume, totaling 464 titles, comprising 11,328 volumes. However, between the summer and autumn of 1918 of the Republic Era, the bandit Wang Jinfal occupied Liaocheng twice, resulting in significant losses to the collection. When the Department of Education dispatched personnel to investigate thoroughly in the winter, only five Song dynasty editions and seventeen Yuan dynasty editions remained, with the rest being fine Ming and Qing dynasty editions. The so-called "fine editions" are the common editions of the Haiyuan Pavilion. However, most of the fine Song and Yuan dynasty editions had been transported to Tianjin by the owner Yang Jingfu for safekeeping before the bandits occupied Liaocheng, and were not lost. What was lost were mostly the common books of the Haiyuan Pavilion. In the spring of last year, when the Department of Civil Affairs and the Department of Education were about to take steps to preserve the collection, the war suddenly broke out, and Liaocheng was occupied by Wang Jinfal again. During the eight months of occupation, the bandits sold many of the books. When they left in the autumn, they took another portion of the collection with them, which is now scattered in Baoding, with the titles unknown. Some of the books that were sold have been appearing in Jinan from time to time. The Shandong Library has purchased four titles, spending a total of 215 yuan: Feng Shi Wen Jian Ji, collated by Huang Raopu, Zhu Qiuyai, He Yimen, and He Xiaoshan; Jiang Huai Yi Ren Lu, hand-copied by Wu Meian and collated by Huang Raopu; Wu Yi Xin Ji, a Ming dynasty edition; and a calligraphy album written jointly by Liu Wuzhong and his brothers. The ink on these books is still fresh and new, making them truly valuable. There are also several titles of Lin Hejing's collected works, which were reportedly purchased in Qingdao by a certain mayor for 590 yuan. Yang Jingfu sold twelve titles in Tianjin, including the best Song dynasty edition of the Shi Cai Tang edition of Meng Dongye Ji, Meng Xiangyang Ji, Gai Jia Zhou Ji, and Liu Liuzhou Ji, totaling less than thirty volumes. Ye Yuhu and Zhang Daishan jointly offered 60,000 yuan for them, but they were not sold. They were eventually purchased by a Japanese person for 80,000 yuan, through the introduction of a Beijing bookseller named Wang. The Japanese person used gold certificates to purchase the books, as the price of gold was high, so they did not consider the price to be expensive. Last autumn, when the provincial army recovered Liaocheng, the elderly Mrs. Yang transported all of the remaining books to Jinan for safekeeping, totaling fifty-seven cases, mostly containing extremely fine Ming dynasty editions. This represents not only a drop in the ocean compared to the original Haiyuan Pavilion collection, but also only what was left since Zeng. The rare Song and Yuan dynasty editions were all transported to Tianjin by Yang Jingfu. The Ministry of Education has repeatedly telegraphed the Provincial Government and the Department of Education to pay attention to this matter. The Provincial Government's Standing Committee decided to order the Department of Civil Affairs and the Department of Education to handle the matter. The Department of Civil Affairs dispatched an inspector to Dongxing Lane in the concession area to visit the owner, the elderly Mrs. Yang. A certain gentleman acted as her representative, stating that the books were in disarray when they were transported from Dongchang to Jinan, and that they would invite inspection after they had been organized, which was essentially a rejection. A committee member from the Department of Education directly presented three conditions to the elderly Mrs. Yang. The first option was for the Yang family to donate the entire collection. This option was further divided into three sub-options: (1) The National Government and the Provincial Government would issue a clear decree stating that the ownership of the books would forever belong to the Yang family; (2) A Haiyuan Pavilion Library would be built to display the books for public viewing; (3) A Book Committee would be organized to manage the library, with representatives from the National Government, the Provincial Government, and the Yang family, with the Yang family serving as the chairman. All revenue from entrance tickets to the library and from the reproduction of the books would belong to the Yang family. The National Government would also be requested to issue a commendation to the Yang family. The second option was a semi-donation and semi-sale. The Yang family's books would first be displayed and a catalog compiled. Hu Shi, Yuan Tongli, Fu Zengxiang, and others would be invited to Jinan to inspect and assess the books. The final price would be determined by the majority opinion. For example, if the assessed price was 1 million yuan, the government would give the Yang family 500,000 yuan, and the remaining 500,000 yuan would be considered a donation by the Yang family. This option would also involve building a Haiyuan Pavilion Library, and because the Yang family would be donating 500,000 yuan, the National Government and the Provincial Government would also be petitioned to issue a commendation. The third option was for the government to purchase the entire collection after valuation. The Yang family could choose any of these three options, and could also propose other options for discussion. If the Yang family still wished to preserve the collection privately as before, that would also be acceptable. However, if they were to sell the collection, the Shandong Library would have the right of first refusal. If the Yang family were to sell the collection privately, the government would be able to intervene. After receiving these conditions, the elderly Mrs. Yang seemed open to discussion, but the matter was of great importance and needed to be resolved by a family meeting, and Lao Zhichang (Yang Jingfu's father-in-law) would be asked to come to Jinan to make a decision. It is said that the National Government and the Provincial Government have made preparations for the second and third options, and that funding would not be a problem. The decision depends solely on the Yang family's response. Haiyuan Pavilion books are still frequently appearing on the market in Jinan, indicating that sales are continuing.

He Chengjun Returns to Wuhan

Hankou Dispatch: He Chengjun, Director of the Wuhan Pacification Headquarters, returned to Hankou today (1st) via China National Aviation Corporation's "Wuchang" plane from Nanjing, where he had gone to consult with Chiang Kai-shek regarding bandit suppression strategies. Due to a flight delay, he did not arrive until 4:15 PM. He was accompanied by He Jingwu, Director of the Pinghan Railway Bureau. After disembarking, He immediately went to the headquarters of the Third Army Corps, and then summoned Fang Benren, Wu Xingya, Liu Wendao, Xu Yuanquan, Wang Jinyu, Ji Hongchang, Zhang Yinxiang, Xiao Zhichu, Hua Wenxuan, and others to discuss all matters. This reporter drove to visit him and was received by He, who made the following statement: "During my visit to Nanjing, I discussed concrete measures for bandit suppression in the three provinces with the Commander-in-Chief. Minister He Yingqin will soon go to Nanchang. It is not yet known whether he will come to Hankou, but the Wuhan Pacification Headquarters will continue to be responsible for directing bandit suppression affairs in the three provinces as before. Huang Shaohong, after arriving in Nanjing, has already agreed on a proper settlement of the Guangxi affair. I have met with Huang Shaohong and Chen Jitang, and know that Li Bai and others are still sincere, so there are no problems in resolving the Guangxi affair. Regarding the settlement of the Sichuan affair, representatives of Liu Wenhui, Deng Xihou, and Tian Songyao have all arrived in Nanjing. I, along with Zhang Qun, Shao Lizi, and others, introduced the representatives to the Commander-in-Chief. The Central Government has decided to handle the Sichuan affair with leniency and peace. The representatives have all expressed their sincere obedience, and concrete solutions will be available within days. Regarding the implementation of the business tax in Hankou, we will follow the orders of the Central Government and consult with all sectors of Hankou to proceed, aiming for mutual assistance and mutual benefit. In addition, I have discussed the Hubei Province Disaster Relief Bond Regulations with President Hu of the Legislative Yuan, and it is hoped that they will be passed." At this point, He was fatigued from his flight and feeling unwell, so this reporter took his leave. (February 1st)

Northeast Railway Transportation Conference

▲Participants Include Ten Railways Including Beining and Sitao

▲Opening Ceremony Scheduled for the 2nd of This Month

Shenyang Dispatch: The core of the railway business lies in passenger and freight transportation. Due to special circumstances, the regulations for passenger and freight transportation on various railways in the Northeast either follow the ministerial guidelines or imitate foreign railways, making adjustments for their own advantages and disadvantages. The Northeast Transportation Committee is now convening a Northeast Railway Transportation Conference to unify the regulations of the various railways and promote improvements. The Beining, Sitao, Tao'ang, Qike, Jichang, Jidun, Jihai, Huhai, and Tao Suo railways, and the Shenhai Railway Company have each dispatched the heads of the transportation departments and sections, as well as the relevant personnel in charge, to attend and participate in the discussions. The conference will focus on improving and unifying matters related to passenger and freight transportation. The opening ceremony is scheduled for February 2nd. The Road Administration Division of the Transportation Committee has drafted an outline of 25 items for discussion. The various railways have submitted a total of 87 proposals, including 6 from the Beining Railway, 12 from the Shenhai Railway, 24 from the Sitao Railway, 15 jointly submitted by the Qike and Tao'ang Railways, 16 from the Jidun Railway, 5 from the Jichang Railway, 5 from the Jihai Railway, and 4 from the Huhai Railway. (31st)

Freight Train Derails in Linping on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway

A Shanghai-bound freight train that departed from Zhapu on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway at 10:20 AM today (4th) derailed at Linping Station due to improper switching operations during engine shunting. The locomotive completely derailed, overturned, and damaged the switch and the main line tracks, obstructing through traffic. The details of the incident are as follows:

▲Circumstances of the Locomotive Derailment: The 21st freight train, which departed from Zhapu at 10:20 AM today and was bound for Shanghai, was hauled by locomotive P2 and consisted of 22 freight cars and 2 empty cars. At 1:40 PM, when the train arrived at Linping Station, the locomotive was disconnected for loading and unloading goods and adding cars, and was driven into the No. 2 siding. As it was about to enter the main line, the switchman inadvertently switched the wrong route, causing all six wheels of the locomotive to derail, overturn beside the track, and damage the switch and the main line tracks, obstructing traffic.

▲Station Master Sends Telegram for Assistance: At 2:00 PM, the station master of Linping Station telegraphed the engine plant in Zhapu and the three workshops of the Shanghai Engine and Vehicle Works, as well as all relevant personnel of the railway, reporting the incident and requesting the prompt dispatch of a rescue train.

▲Passenger Trains Delayed: Following the incident, the 7th express train bound for Shanghai, which departed from Zhapu at 3:50 PM, was detained at Kuanqiao Station. The 9th overnight express train bound for Shanghai, which departed from Zhapu at 5:40 PM, was also detained at Jianqiao Station. The 6th slow train bound for Hangzhou from Shanghai, which departed at 9:20 AM, was detained at Xucun Station. All of these trains will be able to pass only after the damaged tracks at Linping Station are repaired.

▲Engine Plant Dispatches Rescue Train: At 2:47 PM, Chen Mingshou, director of the engine plant at Zhapu Station, accompanied by Jiang Shenghua of the Hangzhou Section of the Engineering Department, Mr. Ding Mengshi (transliteration), a Westerner and head of the Traffic Department, and Huang Shousong, the station affairs inspector, led more than 30 employees of the engine and engineering departments on a special train, carrying a crane, jacks, rails, and all necessary equipment. Upon arriving at Linping, Chen Mingshou, Jiang Shenghua, and others consulted and decided to lay a temporary track next to the siding in order to use jacks to first move the derailed locomotive water tank. After the damaged track is repaired, the derailed front end of the locomotive will be jacked back onto the track. The repair is expected to be completed and traffic restored by 7:30 PM.

▲Tracks Now Repaired: The 7th express train and the 9th overnight express train that departed from Hangzhou for Shanghai today were both detained at Jianqiao. At approximately 8:00 PM, the track at Linping was reported to have been repaired, and the two passenger trains were connected and departed from Jianqiao. It is estimated that they will arrive in Shanghai at approximately 1:00 AM tomorrow (5th). The 6th slow train from Shanghai to Hangzhou, which was detained at Xucun Station, also departed from Xucun at the same time. All of the above passenger trains are delayed by more than five hours. All freight trains in both directions will have to wait until tomorrow to reach their respective stations.

Local Communications

Jinshan

Detailed Report on the Rampant Bandits in Jinshan: The bandit leaders Taibao A Shu, Zhuluo A Mei, Lu Yaosheng, and Wang A Jiu are the "Four King Kongs" of the Jinshan gang of bandits. They have over a thousand men under their command, with Jinshanwei, Qianjiaxu, and Nanlu being their main bases. All towns and villages in Jinshan have been looted, with some towns being looted three or four times. Even farmers who barely have enough to eat have not been spared. Each month, these gangs of bandits also openly loot in Songjiang and Pinghu, returning fully loaded with spoils and dividing the loot without any hesitation. Recently, the major and minor leaders have been forcibly taking captured women from good families as their wives and concubines. Last month, bandit leader Lu Yaosheng hosted a banquet for a concubine that one of his bandits had taken. A bandit scout reported that two petty thieves had been captured for impersonating bandits and extorting money. Lu was furious and ordered them to be executed. As his men were pushing them out to be bound, a small number of soldiers passed by on patrol. Fearing that the situation would be exposed, Lu released the two petty thieves. It is said that the internal organization of the various gangs is very tight. In addition to the bandit leader serving as commander, there are ranks of division commander, battalion commander, staff officer, and secretary. Gu, the secretary of Taibao A Shu, was the secretary-general of Li Yi'e two years ago. They are also well-supplied with firearms, including machine guns and Mauser pistols, which are secretly smuggled back from Shanghai in successive shipments. Last autumn, the rice crop in the county was excellent, but due to the impact of the slogan "Do Not Return Rent," landowners have moved away, leaving the fields unattended. The county magistrate is only concerned with protecting the county government, and ignores the banditry in the countryside. Although the county is garrisoned by an army, with one battalion and one company stationed, they are unfamiliar with the area and people, and cannot capture any bandits even if they want to conduct a large-scale search.

Furthermore, on the 30th of last month, a gang of over a hundred bandits suddenly arrived in Ganxiang Town, which belongs to Jinshan County. They first seized weapons from the Public Security Bureau, and then claimed to borrow 18,000 yuan from the pawnshops and rice shops, demanding that the money be delivered to the Qilong Temple, three miles from the town, within three days. The township head of the town's district government and the head of the Public Security Bureau went to the county the next day to ask for instructions, but returned disappointed as the county government was helpless. They also consulted with the water police, but they refused to go as they had not received orders from above. There are no wealthy households in the town, so how can such a large sum be raised? The entire town is in a state of fear, and faces certain death.

Suzhou

The Case of Neglect of Duty by the Head of the Defense Corps: On the evening of July 1st of last year, Cai Guoqing, the driver of Cai Xiong-yao, head of the Beicai Town Defense Corps in Nanhui County, reported to the corps headquarters that there was a counterfeiting operation in the Zhang family ancestral hall nearby. Cai Xiong-yao immediately led over ten members of the defense corps to search the hall, along with the head of the Xueqiao Township Defense Corps. Upon arriving at the destination, because the Zhang family ancestral hall was quiet, they did not enter, and soon returned to town. On the outskirts of town, they apprehended He Bingyuan and Shi Xiaogou, two individuals with suspicious appearances, and interrogated them briefly. As the interrogation revealed no connection to the crime, they were released the next morning. Tang Zhilian, a resident of the town, learned of the incident and suspected that Cai Xiong-yao had been bribed to release the suspects. She filed a complaint with the Nanhui County government. The county government summoned Cai to the county government for questioning and took him into custody. In November, he was sentenced to one year of imprisonment and ten years of deprivation of civil rights. Cai refused to accept the judgment and retained lawyer Pan Chenge to appeal to the High Court. Yesterday (4th), the Third Criminal Court heard the case and announced the end of the debate, with a verdict scheduled for the 9th of this month.

A Reactionary Commits Himself to the High Court: Cao Qiheng, a 21-year-old woman from Jiangdu, worked at the Qingzhenghui (Youth Rectification Society) in Jiangdu in 1929. After the Qingzhenghui ceased operations, she studied at Yangzhou High School. Cao Qiheng had an older brother named Cao Qijin, who joined the Communist Party in 1927. He forced his younger sister Qiheng to join as well. At the time, Qiheng was forced to join because she was unable to resist her brother. Later, Qijin fled due to increased surveillance and has not returned home. After her brother left, Cao Qiheng realized her mistake and came to Suzhou yesterday (4th) to commit herself to the High Court. Zhu, the prosecutor of the High Court Procuratorate, immediately opened a trial to investigate the matter.

Wuxi

Successive Water and Land Robberies Occurring During This Winter Defense Period, Robberies Are Rampant in Rural Areas. Unexpectedly, Yesterday, Three Robberies Occurred Continuously on Water and Land: (1) Pu Renbao, a resident of Gu Xi, Nanfangquan, District 14, makes a living by farming and also works as a pig trader. Last month, he hired a boat, loaded dozens of large pigs, and transported them to Dongting Xishan for sale. After selling them all, Pu Renbao, to avoid the danger of bandits in the lake, carried the money and took a steamer to Suzhou, then transferred to a train to return to Wuxi. Zhang Apei, on the other hand, sailed back to Wuxi yesterday. Unexpectedly, when he reached the area near Jiaozhu in Taihu Lake, two bandit boats suddenly appeared, and more than twenty Hunan bandits jumped out, holding several box cannons. They boarded the boat and searched it, robbing two cotton quilts, two silver dollars, and two fur coats belonging to a passenger named Jia. (2) The home of the widow Hua Chen in Xiaoqiao Tou, Nanyan City, was suddenly visited by three bandits at about 2 a.m. last night. Each of them carried a handgun and a flashlight. They broke into the house and robbed three gold bracelets, more than ten silver bracelets, and ten leather jackets, worth about 500 silver dollars. (3) Wang, a mechanic from Nanqiao Town, Yangming Township, came to the city to shop yesterday. At about 4 p.m., he was walking back to his hometown when, unexpectedly, when he reached the Xianli Dun Bridge, three thugs suddenly chased after him from behind, blocked his way, pulled out handguns, and searched his entire body. They robbed a wallet containing 84 silver dollars. After getting the loot, the thugs scurried away. Inspector Zhou Runshi Was Arrested in the Town. Zhou Runshi, a police inspector specially sent to Wuxi by the Civil Affairs Department, stayed at the New World Hotel, frequented prostitutes, and was also involved in a case of adultery and abduction of Shen Xiang's concubine, a local resident. It is now known that after Zhou Runshi fled Suzhou, he went to Zhenjiang the day before yesterday (the 2nd). At about 10 a.m., Zhou went to the Police Academy outside the South Gate to see the principal, Wang Dasui, expressed his remorse, and requested that the case be made up. Principal Wang was furious and immediately rebuked him severely. He also reported the matter to Hu, the head of the Civil Affairs Department, by telephone and asked for instructions. Minister Hu, according to the phone call, instructed to have Zhou watched and escorted to the department for investigation. At 11 a.m., Principal Wang escorted Zhou to the Civil Affairs Department. Minister Hu immediately issued an order to have the provincial guard watch over him. At 4 p.m., Zhai Hongda, a member of the Third Section of the Civil Affairs Department, brought Zhou out for questioning. Zhou confessed that he had indeed frequented prostitutes at the New World Hotel in Wuxi, introduced by Wang Chongxi, the director of the Eighth Sub-bureau. After finishing his official business, he went to Suzhou, where Qin Enrui, a member of the Third Sub-bureau, bought the train ticket for him. After arriving in Suzhou, he met Zhou Xingzhen. Because of their hometown relationship, they were acquainted. She said that she had left home in a fit of anger because of a family quarrel. He took her to the Dongwu Hotel, but there was no case of adultery or abduction. After the interrogation, he was sent back into custody. Minister Hu of the Civil Affairs Department believed that since Zhou Runshi had been arrested, he should be brought to justice as soon as possible. Therefore, he specially telegraphed Pan, the county magistrate of this county, ordering him to immediately summon all the witnesses and bring them to the court for questioning. After receiving the order, County Magistrate Pan immediately instructed Director Xu of the Public Security Bureau to comply. After receiving the order, Director Xu dispatched police officers yesterday (the 4th) afternoon to summon the plaintiff Shen Xiang, Zhou Xingzhen, and the local prostitute Wang Lihong to the bureau to await transfer to the county. However, Wang Chongxi, the director of the Eighth Sub-bureau, and Qin Enrui, a member of the Third Sub-bureau, had to wait until Zhou Runshi was escorted to Wuxi before they could be summoned for questioning. As for Wang Shiyi, the patrol officer of the Third Public Security Bureau of Suzhou, who was suspected of showing favoritism and privately releasing Zhou Runshi, it was feared that he would also have to be summoned for questioning when necessary. In addition, after the case occurred, Director Xu of the Public Security Bureau believed that Wang Chongxi and Qin Enrui, as public security personnel, dared to engage in debauchery and frequent prostitutes, and specially submitted a report to the county government for approval. County Magistrate Pan, after receiving the report, issued a reply yesterday, saying, "Having read the report, Wang Chongxi should be dismissed from his position in advance. The vacancy is approved to be filled by Zhou Jiashan returning to his post, and the date of replacement should be reported for investigation. The officer and Qin Enrui are both incumbent police officers, but they are engaging in debauchery and frequenting prostitutes, and do not know how to restrain themselves. It is extremely absurd and should be submitted to the Civil Affairs Department for punishment to set an example."

Four Suicide Cases in One Day In recent days, suicide cases have been heard frequently in this county. The reasons are mostly economic pressure or quarrels, leading to anger and resentment. Unexpectedly, four suicide cases occurred again the day before yesterday. The details are as follows: (1) Yan Bingjun, a resident of Zhaimen, about five miles north of Zhangjingqiao Town, District 7 (Huai Shang), was 21 years old. In the 17th year of the Republic of China, he married A'da (21 years old), the daughter of the late Yuan Qingchen of Hetangqiao in the same district, through a matchmaker. After she entered the family, the couple were on good terms. Recently, Bingjun's elder sister, Xiudi, suddenly had a disagreement with her sister-in-law, Yuan, at home. She then sowed discord in front of Bingjun, causing quarrels between the couple from time to time. Yuan, filled with anger and resentment, suddenly had the idea of ​​ending her life. On the morning of the day before yesterday, at about 8 o'clock, she hanged herself in the room without anyone knowing. (2) Wang, the wife of Zhao Xiangbao, a villager in Zhaojiatang, about two miles northwest of Zhangjingqiao Town in the same district, who was in her twenties, suddenly hanged herself after quarreling with her aunt the day before yesterday. (3) Zhang Yunquan, also known as Yongquan, the owner of the Xieheshun clothing store at the south end of Shengxiang Bridge in the city, was already in his sixties. His wife, Tong, had two sons who were already married. Tong was naturally fierce and often had disputes with her two daughters-in-law. Yunquan often sided with his daughters-in-law, which caused quarrels between the couple from time to time. Yunquan, out of anger, suddenly had the idea of ​​committing suicide. On the day before yesterday, he swallowed several qian of raw opium and several bottles of sedative water. By the time it was noticed, it was too late to save him. (4) Wang Sixi, a 17-year-old apprentice at Lisheng Tea and Preserved Fruit Shop on Tongyun Road outside Guangfu Gate, also swallowed two pieces of red arsenic and four pieces of white arsenic on the morning of the day before yesterday for some unknown reason. After the shop owner noticed, he immediately sent him to the Brothers Hospital for treatment, and he was able to turn the corner.

Changzhou

An Elderly Man with White Hair Was Assassinated. The body of an elderly man with white hair was found in a wheat field in Lujia Yao Feng, Xiaping Bridge, outside the East Gate of the First District of Wuyi County. There were six or seven knife wounds on the top of his head, and his brains were flowing out. Three days later, the district office reported it to the County Court Procuratorate. Yang Kongxi, the chief prosecutor, led the inspection officials to examine the body. The examination confirmed that he died from multiple knife wounds. He ordered the local security chief to prepare a coffin for the body and instructed the police to investigate the criminal involved in the case.

The Knife Society is Dissolved. Recently, many Knife Society groups have been discovered in various townships of Wuyi County. After Zhang, the county magistrate, learned about this, he raised the issue for discussion at the district chief meeting on the 2nd. It was decided that the county government would issue a notice to dissolve them. If there was any resistance, it would be resolved by force. Today (the 4th), the county government has implemented the decision.

Jiading

The Zhenhu Provincial Road is Re-routed. The originally planned route of the Zhenhu Provincial Road entered the country through Taicang County, passed outside the West Gate to Nanxiang, and then reached Shanghai in the southeast. A few days ago, Qiu Xijue, the director of the County Construction Bureau, took a car to the province to discuss with the provincial department. It was heard that the Taicang-Jiading section would follow the originally planned route and construction would begin soon. The provincial government also felt that the planned route for the Jiading-Shanghai section was not very appropriate. Director Qiu had already determined another route, bypassing the North Gate from the West Gate and connecting with the Jialuo Motor Road to reach Shanghai directly. He submitted it to the provincial department for approval, and the instruction has been received for approval.

The Xu Cheng Road is Extended Northward. The road between Xuhang and Chengqiao in the eastern township was dilapidated. Previously, Deng Weixin and Lu Jianru and others initiated the repaving of the cobblestone road, which has been completed. The road between Xuhang and Liuhe is also rugged and narrow, making travel inconvenient. Now, fundraising is also underway to extend it northward. It is heard that it will first be built to Tanshiqiao, which will cost about a thousand silver dollars.

Changshu

Bandits Attempt to Rob the Seventh District Town. The Seventh District of this county is adjacent to Huadang, and bandits often come and go. Last month, four families were robbed. In order to repair the fold after the sheep were stolen, the Public Security Bureau immediately added 20 water police officers and dispatched three patrol boats from Wangshi to station in the southern countryside. Unexpectedly, at 8:30 p.m. on the 2nd, more than a dozen boats approached from Huadang and landed at Shenbang, intending to rob the Jin Shaofu family there. When the bandits arrived, a large boat guided them and blew a police whistle as a signal. The bandits had box cannons, handguns, rifles, and short knives. After landing, they fired several shots as a show of force. However, the villagers there were wary after the last major robbery. Moreover, the time was still early, and the villagers had not yet gone to bed. Suddenly hearing gunshots, they knew that something had happened and immediately beat gongs to warn everyone. Unexpectedly, the bandits still did not retreat and fired more densely. At this time, they were heard by the defense forces of the district, who rushed out to fight back. The bandits then returned to their boats. The civilians also used telephones to call for reinforcements from neighboring villages such as Lianqi, Xin'an, and Mocheng, and asked them to set off to encircle and suppress the bandits. After receiving the calls, each village advanced toward Shenbing. However, the bandit boats had already escaped into the lake. One of the bandit boats suddenly encountered an armed group from the timber raft depot, and both sides exchanged several shots. As a result, the bandit boats turned and fled into Zhou Dang (Suzhou territory).

The County Annals are Re-edited. The county annals of this county were previously edited by Ding Zuyin (Zhisun), a local resident. After Ding's death last year, there was no one to take charge of the editing. The county government believed that the county annals could not be suspended and appointed Xu Zhaowei, a historian, to continue the editing. Xu has agreed.

Nantong

The Pacification Office is Abolished. The Jiangsu Pacification Superintendent combined the military, political, and police organs of Nantong to form a Pacification Office. The matters handled by the office were all duties of the joint defense district chief, pacification district commander, and county magistrate and public security bureau chief, which were similar to parallel organs and prone to abuses. An order was issued to abolish the establishment.

The Liang Department Established an Inspection Office. Liang Guanying, the commander of the Twenty-fifth Route, dispatched his troops to Tongzhou for pacification. Because Tongzhou was located on the river and sea, and bandits could easily come and go, he appointed Zhu Guoheng as the director of the Tongzhou Inspection Office. The office was located at Xisi Temple in the south of the city. Inspection teams were stationed at various ports and key passes.

The County Government Investigated and Reported Political Prisoners Eligible for Amnesty. The county government received an order from the provincial government to investigate and report within ten days the names of prisoners in custody who were eligible for the New Year's Day amnesty. County Magistrate Zhang was currently investigating the case in Zixiang. It was found that there were more than ten prisoners in custody on charges of counter-revolution, and a report was submitted for approval.

The Tobacco Smoking Case of Telegraph Bureau Employees Was Judged. Zhang Lin and Xu Xiaotian, employees of the Nantong Telegraph Bureau, smoked opium in the bureau. Zhu Ronggui, a prosecutor of the County Court, went to investigate and apprehended the witnesses. He filed a public prosecution, and the Criminal Court sentenced Zhang and Xu to one month of imprisonment and fined them sixty yuan each. The Su Wolf Soldiers Field Requested Instructions for Handling. The Ministry of Military Affairs ordered the county government to follow the National Government's order and first order the Tonghai Reclamation Company to pay the price for encroaching on the Suzhen Langshan two battalion soldiers fields. If they were unwilling to comply, it should be auctioned and closed. County Magistrate Zhang presented a report to the ministry requesting instructions for handling because the company had not yet sent a person in charge to the county government to make a statement.

Yangzhou

The Elementary School Strike Has Not Yet Been Resolved. The strike for wages in Jiangdu has been brewing for three weeks. As of today (the 3rd), there is still no news of resumption of classes. It is recently heard that the county government has reached the end of its rope in terms of fundraising. Beyond two and a half months, there is really no surplus capacity to raise more funds. The principals of the schools in the urban area also realize that this matter is not easy to resolve satisfactorily. Therefore, the principals of each school are raising funds separately. It is recently heard that the principals of each school can raise about 3,000 yuan. If this money is raised, the urban area can issue half a month's salary more. Then, the principals of each school will separately communicate with the teachers in their respective districts to start classes first. However, the Teachers Association suddenly sent a letter to the Principals Association today, stating that there were still points to be considered regarding the treatment issue. The letter said, "Because the two issues of arrears in salary and treatment have not been satisfactorily resolved, the association unanimously decided on February 2 to submit a letter of resignation to the Principals Association. Of course, the classwork section cannot be responsible. It is hoped that all colleagues will adhere to their original intentions and unite as one." Whether classes can be resumed this week is still unknown.

Jiaxing

The National Exhibition Closed. The National Goods Mobile Exhibition initiated by the Jiaxing County Government and various groups decided to hold the exhibition for two weeks. The term has now expired, so a banquet was held on the 3rd to entertain all sectors of society. The venue was at Qingfeng Hall. During the banquet, Shen Guisun and Ni Zhuan distributed Mei Lanfang, Bai Jinlong, and Great Wall cigarettes, as well as domestic enamel tea trays, to the guests. Sun Choucheng said, "When I came to He with the representatives on the 18th, I was welcomed by all sectors of society, which is enough to show their enthusiasm for promoting national goods. I am very sorry that I am unable to stay in He to assist due to my busy schedule." It was then decided to load the goods on the 5th and return to Shanghai on the 6th, and the meeting was adjourned.

Shaoxing

The Qianqing Fourteen Village Association Raises Funds to Build Roads. Qianqing in Shaoxing borders Xiaoshan County on the west and north. The people of the two counties often have disputes because the boundary roads are unclear. Now, the Qianqing Fourteen Village Association, which is related to the Shatuan Land in Xiatuan, has initiated a joint organization committee to raise large sums of money to build boundary roads for clarity. They have drafted articles of association and plans and submitted them to the Shaoxing and Xiaoshan county governments and the Department of Civil Affairs for approval and implementation. The planned road is thirty li long, and construction has already begun. It is scheduled to be completed on February 15. The total construction cost is more than 7,200 silver dollars. By donating one jiao of silver per mu from the more than 69,000 mu of Shatuan Land in Xiatuan, 6,900 silver dollars can be obtained. The shortfall will be shared by the fourteen villages.

Xiaoshan

Dispatch Personnel to Organize the Autonomous Household Donation. The Xiaoshan County Government believes that if the collection of autonomous household donations by the village committee is not organized, it will not be enough to serve as a basis for accounting. Personnel have been dispatched to organize the work and a notice has been issued. At the same time, each district office is ordered by telegram to take responsibility for assistance and not to collect donations from the village committee or the township and town preparatory office to clarify the boundaries and provide assistance for organization. Detailed registration should be completed quickly and the monthly income and expenditure statements should be reported for verification.

Suicide Case of a Woman in Zhongzhuang Village. There was a woman named Zhao Caiqin in Zhongzhuang Village outside the South Gate of Xiaoshan. Her father died early and she had no brothers. This year, she was studying at a school in Shanghai. Because she and a classmate, Wang, were in love, they privately agreed to marry. Unexpectedly, her mother found out about it and ordered Caiqin to drop out of school and return home, where she was strictly controlled. The woman, unable to have free love, had the idea of ​​committing suicide. On the night of January 28, she committed suicide by drinking salt brine. By the time it was noticed, her soul had already gone to the underworld. Her mother regretted it too late and cried bitterly.

Ningbo

Foreign Minister Wang and His Wife Left Ningbo for Beijing. Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting and his wife arrived at Ningbo on the Xinjing steamer from Shanghai on the morning of the 1st. They took a car to Cixi to visit his father-in-law, Shi Yueming, for his 70th birthday. Foreign Minister Wang originally planned to celebrate his birthday in Cixi and then travel to Fenghua, his hometown. Unexpectedly, he received a telegram from Nanjing in Cixi yesterday, saying that Mo Dehui was expected to arrive in Beijing on the 3rd. Therefore, Foreign Minister Wang was scheduled to rush back to Nanjing today (the 3rd) to discuss the Sino-Russian incident with Mo.

Ningbo Merchants Oppose the Increase in Freight Charges by the Four Wheel Company. Ningbo commercial organizations believe that this time, the Sanbei Merchants Taikoo Ningshao Four Wheel Shipping Company, under the pretext of adding a convoy, not only increased passenger freight charges but also increased round-trip cargo freight charges by 20%, which is actually taking advantage of the name to seek profits. Moreover, freight charges had already been increased once last year, so it is impossible to agree to another increase this time. Therefore, the commercial organizations decided to express their opposition at the Commercial Statistics Conference yesterday afternoon.

Miscellaneous Records of Robbery Cases. In Hejin Pier, Xixiang, Yin County, the family of Lu Quanlin, a resident, was suddenly visited by five bandits the night before last. Three of them broke in through the front door, and two guarded the back door. The bandits who entered the door did not rob anything. They tied up Quanlin's youngest son (only eight months old) and demanded a ransom of 6,000 yuan. In addition, Li Wenying, a customs clerk at the Zhejiang Customs of Ningbo, was carrying an official document to the county government at about 5 p.m. yesterday. Unexpectedly, while walking in Beiyuelai Lane outside the East Gate, seven or eight bandits saw that Li was carrying a document bag and thought he was delivering banknotes from a bank. One of the bandits immediately punched Li in the face, and another bandit snatched the document bag. Unexpectedly, after opening the bag, they found that it contained account books, so they abandoned the bag and fled. Li was beaten and his nose bled profusely. After the bandits escaped, he reported the incident to the nearby police post with pain. They started searching in different directions, but found nothing.

The First Day of the Shandong Provincial Education Administration Conference

Jinan Dispatch: The Provincial Education Administration Conference held its first regular meeting on the morning of the 2nd, with all 34 members in attendance. Director of Education He Siyuan presided, with Secretary Yang Peng recording the proceedings as customary. Matters reported included: A. Starting from January of this year, the expenses of all schools are to be directly collected from the Finance Department treasury. (Report from the First Section of the Education Department) B. The budget, voucher requests, and blue receipts for the monthly operating expenses of each school should be submitted to the department before the 15th of the previous month for forwarding. (Report from the First Section of the Education Department) C. The qualifications and experience of teaching staff hired by each school must comply with the regulations to avoid rejection. (Report from the Second Section) D. No school should hire students who have not graduated or graduates from unapproved private schools. (Report from the Third Section) Matters discussed: A. It was decided that the daily meeting hours would be from 9:00 AM to 11:00 AM and from 2:00 PM to 4:30 PM. B. On the issue of increasing the efficiency of elementary education, it was decided to assign research to Cai Zisheng, Zhou Chao, Xu Yiqian, Cao Lanzhen, Chen Jianheng, Lai Zhizhong, Zhang Yuguang, etc., with Cai as the convener. C. On the issue of improving vocational education in the province, it was decided to assign research to Meng Xianming, Zhu Jingtang, Wang Chaodong, Dong Zhun, and Zhang Dunna, with Meng as the convener. D. Dong Zhun explained the issue of improving school examination methods. The meeting adjourned at this point.

In the afternoon, at 2:30 PM, the meeting continued. Chairman He Siyuan reported the following matters: A. The income tax to be collected from the teaching staff of each school should be collected monthly starting from January of this year, and receipts should be obtained from the provincial Party headquarters. (Report from the Secretariat) B. When using the operating expenses of each school, it is necessary to adhere to the scope specified in the pre-approved budget, and no transfers between items are allowed. (Report from the Audit Committee) C. The monthly calculation statements of each school must be submitted to the department for forwarding before the 15th of the following month. (Report from the Audit Committee) D. Hereafter, when schools submit registers of teaching staff and students, they should carefully review the contents themselves to avoid rejection by the ministry and delays. (Report from the Second Section) E. The list of books, instruments, specimens, and equipment requested by the department in the previous semester should be submitted promptly (only seven schools, including the Fourth Middle School, Fifth Middle School, Eleventh Middle School, Fifth Normal School, Second Rural Normal School, and Second Experimental Elementary School, have submitted). (Report from the Second Section) Matters discussed: A. On the issue of improving school examination methods, it was decided to assign research to Zhang Yu, Li Taihua, Sun Wei'e, Xu Meisheng, and Yu Guoyuan, with Li as the convener. B. On the issue of principals of provincial schools investigating local education, it was decided to assign research to Sun Wei'e, Feng Peiyuan, Xu Meisheng, Liu Qingtao, Yu Guoyuan, Zhang Yuguang, Zhou Chao, Xu Yiqian, Dong Fengchen, Liu Kunshan, and Lai Zhizhong, with Sun as the convener. C. On the issue of the curriculum and regulations for rural normal schools, it was decided to assign research to the principals of the First, Second, Third, Fourth, and Fourth Rural Normal Schools, and the Education Department inspectors Ma Rufu, Wang Ye, and Lai Zhizhong, with Ma as the convener. The case of whether the length of study for rural normal school students could be changed to four years was combined for discussion. D. On the issue of temporary expenses for the 20th year, it was decided that the Education Department would collect and deliberate on the temporary budget for the 20th year, considering the needs of each school for distribution. E. Local News

Director of the Municipal Education Bureau, Xu Peihuang, Completes Oath of Office

Xu Peihuang, the director of the Shanghai Education Bureau, officially appointed by the National Government, completed his oath of office ceremony at the bureau yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, more than a month after his appointment.

▲ Attendees included Gu Shusen, a special representative from the Ministry of Education, who administered the oath; Mayor Zhang Yuejun, who also attended to give instructions; Tong Xingbai, a representative from the Municipal Party Headquarters; Yu Hongjun, the Secretary-General of the Municipal Government; Chu Minyi, a member of the Central Committee; university presidents Hu Shuhua, Li Zhaohuan, Wang Jingqi, Liu Zhanen, Chu Fucheng, and Ou Yuanhuai; section chiefs and counselors from the Municipal Government Secretariat; bureau chiefs from various bureaus; school principals; representatives from various organizations; and guests, totaling over 400 people, creating a grand occasion. Mayor Zhang served as the chairman, and Yao Gengkui and Chen Duanzhi served as recorders.

▲ Order of the Ceremony: (1) All stand at attention; (2) Sing the Party song; (3) Bow three times to the Party flag, the national flag, and the portrait of the late Premier; (4) The chairman respectfully reads the Premier's will; (5) The oath administrator takes their seat, and the director takes their seat; (6) The mayor presents the seal, and the director receives the seal; (7) The director takes the oath; (8) The oath administrator delivers instructions; (9) Guests give speeches; (10) The director gives a response; (11) Photography; (12) Ceremony concludes with refreshments.

▲ Excerpts from the instructional speech of Gu Yinting from the Ministry of Education: "I am very honored to represent the Ministry of Education in attending Director Xu's inauguration ceremony. Shanghai, as the largest city in the country, has various facilities that attract attention both domestically and internationally. Therefore, Shanghai's education is not only the central hub of the country but should also hold a significant position worldwide. According to educational principles, the education of a metropolis differs from that of ordinary cities or villages. First, attention should be paid to the physical and mental well-being of children because the rapid advancement of industries in the metropolis leads to societal changes. Without careful planning, they often go astray. Major European and American metropolises devote all their efforts to social education for this reason. Take Chicago, for example, which has over seventy elementary schools and public sports fields throughout the city, as well as small parks, small libraries, swimming pools, etc., all distributed throughout the city. This is to ensure that children with vigorous minds and bodies can receive education beyond school education and be introduced to public places for training to avoid the disadvantages of intermittent effort. Secondly, in addition to implementing general education, attention should be paid to special education. Attention should be paid to gifted children, as well as to children with low abilities. Mixed education harms both groups. Thirdly, general schools should pay attention to vocational training so that graduates can cope with urban life. Most importantly, it is necessary to implement the Three Principles of the People education, incorporating the late Premier's teachings into various course materials to create a central ideology. As for reorganizing private schools that promote reactionary ideas through education or those that use education for commercial purposes, they should all be banned. In short, in managing Shanghai's education, one must respond to global trends and consider the special environment. Director Xu has served in the education sector and has worked in the municipal government for many years. He will surely make efforts and contributions to Shanghai's education in the future," and so on.

▲ Excerpts from Mayor Zhang's instructional speech: "I have little experience in education, but every time I participate in various conferences of our Party, I always see that many proposals and declarations relate to education. This shows the Central Government's emphasis on education. I remember that in the political report of the Third National Congress of our Party, there was a passage on education that keenly pointed out the shortcomings of the time. In today's education sector, whether it is students, teachers, school administrators, or administrative staff, everyone feels dissatisfied. Administrative staff are dissatisfied with school administrators, school administrators are dissatisfied with teachers, teachers are dissatisfied with students, students are dissatisfied with schools, and schools are dissatisfied with administrative staff. In this situation of mutual dissatisfaction, the effectiveness of education cannot be seen. Originally, in today's environment, the old cultural foundation has collapsed, and a new cultural foundation has not yet been established. Education has encountered "six difficulties": administration is difficult, funding is difficult, running schools is difficult, finding teachers is difficult, studying is difficult, and advancing to higher education is difficult—everything is difficult. Consequently, there are "four evils": first, education has become a tool for personal gain; second, the result of education is not only the failure to cultivate talent but also the suppression of talent; third, the result of running schools is not only the failure to increase the desire to study but also the possibility of not needing to study; fourth, society has created more unemployed benefit-seekers, causing the country's vitality to be greatly lost. Furthermore, these four evils lead to "three harms": harming individuals, harming society, and harming the country. What kind of outcome will this lead to? Although this is not to say that every school is like this, it is enough to make us vigilant. Therefore, the Third Plenary Session decided to establish the Three Principles of the People as the sole educational purpose of our country. The fundamental issue lies in establishing the culture of the Three Principles of the People, and only then can we promote national prosperity, universal civil rights, and the construction of people's livelihood, achieving concrete results. So, today, I offer this idea as a contribution, hoping that Director Xu can follow this direction to promote the city's education. Director Xu has served in the municipal government for many years and has a proven track record in the education sector. As the head of the Education Bureau, he will surely恪遵 the oath and strive to realize the education of the Three Principles of the People," and so on.

▲ In his speech, Tong Xingbai, the representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, stated, "Our city has a vast area. I hope Director Xu will focus on the overall development, especially emphasizing rural education and labor education," and so on. Next, Hu Shuhua, Chu Fucheng, Wang Yun, and other gentlemen gave speeches. Due to their length, they are omitted here.

▲ Director Xu's reply: "I, Peihuang, have been specially appointed by the Mayor and appointed by the National Government to serve as the Director of the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau. Today, at my oath of office, I am honored to have the representative of the Ministry of Education and the Mayor present to supervise and give instructions, and I have also received guidance from the representative of the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters and representatives from other organizations and guests. Their words are heartfelt, and their teachings to Peihuang are very generous, and their expectations of Peihuang are also very high. After listening respectfully, I am both grateful and ashamed. I especially apologize for the cramped meeting hall and the inadequate reception, which has caused many oversights. Peihuang hereby sincerely accepts everyone's instructions, vows to follow them with all my strength, and earnestly implements them. I will also briefly present my development plan for the city's education to everyone, hoping for your correction and guidance: (1) One of the most important tasks for the Bureau at present is to reorganize existing undertakings. The Bureau has had frequent changes in leadership in the past three and a half years. Although the Bureau's work has progressed year by year, the superficiality of its effectiveness and the confusion of its threads are undeniable. The way to reorganize is to grasp the key points—the so-called 'to shake a garment, one must lift its collar; to raise one's eyes, one must grasp the rope.' Summarizing what is currently underway, there are several aspects as follows:

A. "Nimble communication between the Bureau and its affiliated organizations." The Bureau's affiliated organizations, considering only the municipal primary and secondary schools and community schools, already number more than 290. Previously, relations were scattered, and communication was minimal. Usually, there was little interaction outside of official business. Peihuang is now striving to improve this, aiming to make the relationship between the Bureau and the schools like that between a family and its children, becoming increasingly close so that in the event of an accident, they are as interconnected as a hand directing an arm or an arm directing a finger, with no more concern about separation, just as the ancients said, 'Those who are high in the hall and far from the curtain must ensure that they absolutely no longer exist.' The Bureau, based on this intention, in addition to increasing inspections, also makes the heads and principals of each affiliated organization meet and talk with the staff of the Bureau to communicate and break down the previous sense of separation, and in terms of handling affairs, it also strives for speed so that everything is communicated, and no cases are left unresolved.

B. "Performance evaluation of various undertakings." All undertakings value specialization, so it's important to know whether the handling of undertakings is appropriate and the level of performance in handling undertakings is high or low. In terms of undertakings, this can be used as a model; in terms of those handling undertakings, this can also be used for reward and punishment. The use of performance evaluation is not only for passive warning but also for active guidance. The Bureau's undertakings are very tight, and its duties are especially heavy. Peihuang views the development of undertakings as its sole responsibility, holding the purpose of choosing people for tasks, so that undertakings concentrate their strength and increase their effectiveness. With no wasted talent, there is no wasted work. With no wasted work, success can be achieved quickly. The Bureau is currently operating in this spirit in various businesses. Perhaps the drawbacks of leakage can be washed away.

C. "Increasing the efficiency of internal and external affairs." The efficiency of handling various affairs is high, resulting in twice the results with half the effort, with fewer people and less cost. Low efficiency results in half the results with twice the effort, with more people and greater cost. However, to increase efficiency, those above must supervise and encourage, and those below must work hard, viewing public affairs as private. The Bureau is now working in this spirit, aiming to increase the efficiency of internal and external affairs. The performance evaluation of various undertakings mentioned earlier also aims to increase efficiency.

D. "All undertakings must conform to regulations." The purpose of setting up regulations is to enable people to follow them and to ensure that operations have fixed standards to avoid the drawbacks of disorder. If there are regulations but they are not followed, then the regulations are equal to virtual settings, and handling affairs without following the track will inevitably lose its effect. This not only does not conform to the method of scientific management but also does not adapt to the current world trend. What's more, work efficiency will also be reduced, which runs counter to the purpose of increasing efficiency. Therefore, the Bureau will ensure that everything follows the regulations from now on. Regulations are like models, and work is like utensils that have not yet been manufactured. The utensils must be made to match the model, with no difference. If there are regulations that do not conform to the facts, methods should be devised to change them, and there should be no violation. The Bureau strictly adheres to this idea and must seek to ensure that everything is performed according to the truth. In short, in terms of internal and external work, every amount of money must have the effect of that amount, and all the schools and businesses run by the Bureau must be rationalized and scientific. Thus, the school and the business are not worth the burden of the entrustment and the expectations.

(2) In addition to reorganization work, there are also several aspects that are already underway or should be started soon:

A. "Regarding general education." The foundation of the Party and the nation is extremely important, and education is paramount. After the Fourth Plenary Session, the Central Government paid special attention to improving national education. Shanghai, as the center of national education, should follow the educational purpose of the Central Government, which has also been expected by the government and the municipal government, to realize various plans and affairs.

(1) Make the Three Principles of the People permeate the city's education. The Three Principles of the People are the crystallization of the Premier's lifelong revolution to save the country, all-encompassing and all-embracing, and the educational purpose of the Three Principles of the People has also been determined by the government as the sole goal of pursuing education. However, empty words are difficult to be effective. If the true spirit of the principles is not recognized, then the principles cannot be realized. The education sector, having the duty of enlightening the pre-conscious, should especially take the Three Principles of the People as the central belief and set an example to promote their realization so that both teachers and students can have a firm belief and practice them in person, so that they can work together to build the education of the Three Principles of the People. If those who run the city's education can all have the central belief of the Three Principles of the People, then the city's education can have a great development. Only those who can implement it themselves can bear this important responsibility, and leading students can seek to rectify the school spirit and make schools into training places with principles, order, and discipline. Therefore, the Bureau currently focuses on instilling the Three Principles of the People, the late Premier's teachings, in general education. This is regarded as the most important work in the Bureau. In addition to this, what should also be emphasized are:

(2) Scientific education. Among the late Premier's teachings, he brilliantly instructed us to emulate Western methods not by learning their politics, literature, customs, etc., but by learning their science. The world's civilization and the increase in human happiness all originate from the development of science. Only science is the most practical, not advocating empty talk, and using scientific methods to run businesses will inevitably be orderly, planned, and organized, unlike those that are chaotic and patch things up at any time. Therefore, the Bureau will especially focus on scientific education in general education. According to what Japanese educators have said in recent surveys, Japan's education focuses most on science, and the expenses used for scientific equipment account for the largest part of their teaching expenses. Compared to our country, the scientific education equipment of our country's universities is still lacking. A photo of Xu Peihuang, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau, taking the oath of office (photographed by Wang Kai)

Is not as good as the equipment of their schools. The equipment of our country's middle schools is not as good as the equipment of their elementary schools. As for our country's elementary schools, they are even less worthy of discussion. How pitiful is this? Therefore, in addition to the Three Principles of the People education, the Bureau focuses on scientific education, striving to gradually add and complete the scientific education equipment in each school, so that even elementary school graduates can have common scientific knowledge. This is not only the most sufficient to increase the general knowledge of the people but also the most beneficial to improving the level of the national people.

(3) Compulsory education. Compulsory education is related to the life of the country and the survival of the nation. The total number of illiterate citizens in our country is over 90%, which is why the people's intelligence is narrow and the people's strength is weak. It is not only insufficient to compete with Europe, America, and Japan but also has infinite obstacles to the construction of the Party and the nation. Therefore, the Fourth Plenary Session attached great importance to compulsory education, which is a crucial plan. Although Shanghai's education is more developed than other places, according to surveys, the number of school-age children enrolled in the city is still less than half, so the promotion of compulsory education should not be delayed. However, to make education universal in the city, it is difficult to achieve without sufficient financial resources. Even if there is funding, it is difficult to find many teachers to run it effectively. Therefore, it is planned to follow the intentions of the Fourth Plenary Session and pilot compulsory education in the Lujiazui district, which has been approved by the Ministry of Education and the municipal government, and then gradually promote it to all districts in the city in the future.

(4) Physical education. Our country has been weak for a long time, and the lack of development of physical education is a reason. The physical education business in the city has made considerable progress in recent years, but I still think it is insufficient. I deeply feel that past physical education businesses have been too focused on students in middle schools and above. In the future, we should strive to make it universal and take elementary schools as the basic training place. Therefore, the Bureau is actively planning the expansion of sports fields and the holding of other physical education businesses.

B. Regarding social education. Social education increases the people's intelligence, nourishes morality, cultivates good citizens, and improves the level of society. Its nature is similar to compulsory education, but compulsory education is limited to children of school age, while social education is mass education, so its impact and effect are even deeper and greater. The Bureau is currently planning three things: (1) After detailed planning in the 19th year, reorganize and expand various community schools and supplementary schools starting from the 20th year to help promote compulsory education; (2) Places for citizens' entertainment are very important. The Fourth Plenary Session has passed a resolution, which has been handed over to the Ministry of Education of the National Government for earnest implementation. Therefore, the Bureau is actively working on the construction of art galleries, concert halls, libraries, museums, and zoos in the Confucius Temple. However, the Bureau's financial and ability are limited, and it deeply hopes that the government and all sectors will provide assistance so that it can be completed as soon as possible; (3) Movies are the greatest auxiliary product of social education, but if they are not used well, they can also become the greatest harm. Recently, there have been more and more events that offend customs and violate the law, and although the reasons are not limited to one end, the influence of movies has also had a great impact. In view of this, the Bureau, in its position of duty, cannot tolerate its horizontal flow and collapse. Therefore, in terms of active improvement, it plans to formulate rules for the production of social education films and request the municipal government and the central government to stipulate award methods. In terms of negative prohibition, it plans to work with relevant bureaus to strictly prohibit the showing of bad Chinese and foreign films or cut them.

In addition, there are two points that the Bureau is also carrying out as part of its policy:

(1) Rewarding and banning private schools. There are so many school-age children in Shanghai, and the municipal treasury's expenses are limited and cannot set up more schools to accommodate them, so we have to rely on private schools to help and make up for the shortcomings of municipal schools. Therefore, the Bureau plans to formulate reward methods for those private schools that have achieved results so that they know where to work hard. Those that have not yet been registered will be urged to improve and register so that they can work together under a consistent education administration system. Those that use schools to earn money and run them corruptly will have to be banned so that society will not be harmed by them. This will reduce the number of illiterates in the positive aspect and destroy the pits that mislead young people in the negative aspect.

(2) Recouping the education rights in the concessions. The Bureau attaches great importance to the education rights in the concessions. The annual income of the Public Concession is three times greater than that of the municipal government, but the expenses for Chinese children's education are very small, and the schools are not in accordance with the Chinese education laws and regulations. The French Concession is also like this. The concession authorities despise Chinese education and ignore Chinese sovereignty. The Bureau cannot ignore this, so it is planning to actively negotiate and will not stop until the goal of recouping is achieved.

The above are the outlines of the Bureau's business plan. It will now first formulate this policy outline and then proceed in order, or advance simultaneously, to ensure that each is realized. This is not only Peihuang's great wish to improve and develop Shanghai's education but also hopes to comfort the central government, the municipal government, and all sectors of society. I am very honored to have you all come together today. I use these words as a voucher for the Bureau's future work and hope that you will give me your advice from time to time.
